<td>                 <dl>                     <dt>You already know your sizes if you own a suit, sportscoat, blazer or tuxedo.</dt><dd>If you currently own one of the above garments and it still fits, simply reference those sizes. They are all items with similar sizing guidelines to suits.</dd><dt>You do not own a  suit, sportscoat, blazer or tuxedo, you do have access to a local tailor shop.</dt><dd>Once again, getting measurements for your suit should be a relatively easy process. You can always visit a local tailor shop to have your measurements taken (NOTE: you should not be charged a fee because the tailor will usually expect you to come back to him for your tailoring/alterations needs).</dd><dt>You do not fit into the previous two categories, but you do own a tape measure and have someone who can measure you.</dt><dd>As long as you have a tape measure and friend/family member, you can easily have your measurements accurately taken.                         <p> Be sure to stand up straight with your arms at your sides. Stand relaxed, yet still erect. Have your friend/family member take the tape measure around your chest (at its fullest part) UNDER your arms. Helpful hint: have your friend/family member insert a finger between the tape measure and your body to ensure a comfortable fit. This would be your "Chest Size". (Ex. 40, 42, 44, etc).</p>                         <p>Next you want to find out if you are a "Short", "Regular", "Long",                             or "X-Long". This is determined by height.<br />                         <br />                         See the chart below, if your height is in the Blue area, you are a short.<br />                         If your height is listed in the red area, you are a regular.<br />                         If your height is listed in the green area, you are a long.<br />                         If your height is taller than 6'3" you are considered to be an X-Long.</p>                          <img alt="sizechart" src="http://www.mensusa.com/sizechart.gif" width="504" height="403" />                      </dd>                      <dd>                         <p>For more assistance, please visit our <a href="http://www.mensusa.com/page3.aspx">Contact Us</a> page.</p>                      </dd>                     </dl>                 </td>             </tr>             <tr>                <td><p style="font-size:18px; font-weight:bold;"><a id="vests" name="vests"></a>Formal Vests:<font waist size should also be factored in.<br /><br /></dt><dd>      <table border="1" bordercolor="#666666" cellpadding="4" cellspacing="8" width="100%">            <tr>         <td name="hats"></a>Hat Size:<font size="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Quick Nav: &nbsp;<a href="#jackets">Jackets/Coats</a>, <a href="#vests">Vests</a></font></p><br /> <dl><dd>      <table border="1" size="1">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Quick Nav: &nbsp;<a href="#jackets">Jackets/Coats</a>, <a href="#vests">Vests</a></font></p> <dl><dt>To measure your collar size:</dt><dd>Take the measurement around the base of your neck and add 1/2 inch to the measurement; this is your "collar size".   </dd><dt>To measure your sleeve length:</dt><dd><table><tr><td><img src="http://www.mensusa.com/template-img/shirtmeasure.jpg" alt="shirt measure" height="180" width="120"></td> <td> A. Base of neck (backside, center)<br /> B. Outside tip of shoulder<br /> C. Outside bend of elbow<br /> D. Wrist or the point at which you prefer the cuff to end<br /><br />  1. Rest your hand on the side of your hip, with elbow bent.<br /><br />  2. Measure as shown in the illustration: - Start at (A) the backside base of the neck, - past (B) the shoulder, - around (C) the elbow, - to (D) the wrist or the point at which you prefer the cuff to end.<br /><br />  The path of the tape measure should follow the outside of the arm.</td></tr></table></dd>   <dt>COMMON MISTAKES:</dt><dd>Some gentleman will measure their "sleeve length" incorrectly because they will start their measurement at the "top of the shoulder" instead of starting at the "middle of the back / bottom of neck".  This can often reduce several inches from your correct measurement.  When this happens, gentleman will sometimes order a 30/31 sleeve instead of the desired longer sleeve length. <br /><br /> For reference, here are some general sizing guidelines regarding "shirt sleeve lengths":<br /><br />  30/31 sleeve = usually 5'5" or shorter<br /> 32/33 sleeve = usually 5'6" to 5'9"<br /> 34/35 sleeve = usually 5'10" to 6'1"<br /> 36/37 sleeve = usually 6'2" to 6'4"<br /> 38/39 sleeve = usually 6'5" or taller<br /><br />  * NOTE: obviously, gentleman come in different shapes and sizes so the above guidelines may not be 100% accurate for everyone; however, it does serve as a good general guideline</dd><dd><p>For more assistance, please visit our <a href="http://www.mensusa.com/page3.aspx">Contact Us</a> page.</p>                 </dd>             </dl>         </td>     </tr> </table>     </div>     <div id="shipping">         If you would like your order to ship faster (UPS Next Day Air, UPS 2nd Day Air ),         complete your purchase and then contact MensUSA.com Customer Service at 1-888-SUIT-USA.     </div>      <div id="Reviews">             <p>Please check our Feedback and buy by confidence.
